[out] {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01ETtEh7UDUzL24N7A7Jb84V","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# medulla\n2\t\n3\t**medulla is a state machine for AI agents.** You describe work as a YAML pipeline — a graph of **nodes** — and medulla runs each node's action on a shell command or an agent harness (`claude-code`, `codex`, `opencode`, `agy`). Bodies emit **signals**; signals route the graph. Built in: retries, fallback to another model, pools with a success threshold, and crash-safe resume.\n4\t\n5\t```\n6\tnode  = action (shell | agent) [× inputs] → signals → next node\n7\tgraph = nodes + on_signal edges + two terminals (__exit_ok__ / __exit_fail__)\n8\t```\n9\t\n10\t**One machine.** Internally every node is a pool: a node without `inputs:` runs over a single phantom input. Policy (timeouts, attempts, fallback) works identically in both modes. The only thing `inputs:` switches is the **signal contract**: without inputs the body talks to the graph (decision node); with inputs the body writes to the manifest and only the join result routes (pool node).\n11\t\n12\t> **Status**: v2 contract (frozen), engine implemented — the v1 engine is **deleted**; v1 pipelines are not supported. `version: \"2\"` is required in every pipeline; the engine rejects anything else with a pointer to the migration table below. Implementation phases: **1** — engine (this document), **2** — harness sessions & run history polish.\n13\t\n14\t## Usage\n15\t\n16\t```bash\n17\tmedulla -w .medulla/pipelines/<name>              # run a pipeline\n18\tmedulla -w ... --var KEY=VALUE                    # set/override vars\n19\tmedulla -w ... --node <name>                      # dev: start from a specific node\n20\tmedulla -w ... --resume                           # continue the latest unfinished run\n21\tmedulla -w ... --run <dir>                        # continue a specific run\n22\tmedulla --docker -w ...                           # run inside the pipeline's Docker image\n23\t```\n24\t\n25\t## Example\n26\t\n27\t```yaml\n28\tversion: \"2\"\n29\tstart: triage\n30\ttimeout: 86400                # whole-run deadline (default 24h; 0 = unlimited)\n31\tvars: {BRANCH: main}\n32\t\n33\tdefaults:                     # policy defaults for every action (\"field absent → take from here\")\n34\t  timeout: 1800\n35\t  fallback: {agent: {harness: claude-code, model: opus}}\n36\t\n37\tnodes:\n38\t\n39\t  # decision node: body signals route the graph\n40\t  triage:\n41\t    shell: |\n42\t      git worktree prune; rm -f .locks/*        # crash-only: clean up on entry\n43\t      n=$(rg -l \"FIXME\" src/ | wc -l | tr -d ' ')\n44\t      [ \"$n\" -gt 0 ] && echo \"<signal:found>ok</signal:found>\" || echo \"<signal:clean>ok</signal:clean>\"\n45\t    timeout: 60\n46\t    on_signal: {found: plan, clean: __exit_ok__}\n47\t\n48\t  plan:\n49\t    agent: {harness: codex, model: gpt-5.5, effort: xhigh}\n50\t    prompt: |\n51\t      {{file:prompts/plan.md}}\n52\t      Branch: {{var:BRANCH}}. Write the plan to plan.md and emit signal planned.\n53\t    max_attempts: 2\n54\t    fallback: {agent: {harness: claude-code, model: sonnet}}\n55\t    on_signal:\n56\t      planned: panel\n57\t      __failed__: __exit_fail__    # body died (rc != 0 after attempts+fallback)\n58\t\n59\t  # pool node: inputs switch the contract — the join routes, bodies write to the manifest\n60\t  panel:\n61\t    inputs:\n62\t      - {slug: gpt5,   harness: codex,       model: gpt-5.5, effort: xhigh}\n63\t      - {slug: sonnet, harness: claude-code, model: sonnet}\n64\t      - {slug: gem,    harness: agy,         model: \"Gemini 3.1 Pro (High)\"}\n65\t    max_parallel: all\n66\t    min_success: 1\n67\t    agent: {harness: \"{{input.harness}}\", model: \"{{input.model}}\", effort: \"{{input.effort:-}}\"}\n68\t    prompt: |\n69\t      You are panelist {{input.slug}} ({{input_index}}/{{input_count}}).\n70\t      Critique the plan: {{file:plan.md}}\n71\t      Write your verdict to reviews/{{input.slug}}.md\n72\t    post: 'test -s \"reviews/{{input.slug}}.md\"'   # verdict = artifact exists, not agent mood\n73\t    on_signal: {__done__: apply}\n74\t\n75\t  apply:\n76\t    inputs: {shell: \"python3 scripts/tickets.py --json\", timeout: 60}\n77\t    max_parallel: 3\n78\t    min_success: 2\n79\t    shell: |\n80\t      bash scripts/fix_one.sh \"$MEDULLA_INPUT_ID\" \"$MEDULLA_INPUT_TITLE\"\n81\t    max_attempts: 2\n82\t    on_signal:\n83\t      __done__: report\n84\t      __empty__: report        # empty queue is legal here — route it explicitly\n85\t\n86\t  report:\n87\t    shell: |\n88\t      ok=$(jq -s 'map(select(.ok))|length' \"$MEDULLA_MANIFEST_APPLY\")\n89\t      total=$(jq -s length \"$MEDULLA_MANIFEST_APPLY\")\n90\t      [ \"$ok\" -eq \"$total\" ] && echo \"<signal:ready>ok</signal:ready>\" || echo \"<signal:rework>ok</signal:rework>\"\n91\t    on_signal: {ready: __exit_ok__, rework: plan}\n92\t```\n93\t\n94\t## Reference\n95\t\n96\t### Pipeline level\n97\t\n98\t| Field | Default | Meaning |\n99\t|---|---|---|\n100\t| `version` | required | must be `\"2\"` |\n101\t| `start` | required | first node |\n102\t| `vars` | `{}` | initial variables (also exported to env; see blacklist below) |\n103\t| `timeout` | 86400 | wall-clock deadline for the whole run; `0` = unlimited. The engine clamps every child timeout to the remaining budget |\n104\t| `defaults` | — | policy defaults for actions: `timeout`, `max_attempts`, `ignore_exit_code`, `fallback`, `on_signal` (per-key merge). Flat scalars only — never merged deep |\n105\t| `keep_runs` | 20 | auto-prune of run history on start |\n106\t\n107\t### Node = action [+ pool] + routing\n108\t\n109\tAction (exactly one of `shell` / `agent`):\n110\t\n111\t| Field | Meaning |\n112\t|---|---|\n113\t| `shell` | shell command; its config *is* the command. `prompt` here is a validation error |\n114\t| `agent` | `{harness, model, effort, args}` — one entity, one block. Scalar shortcut: `agent: codex` ≡ `agent: {harness: codex}`. `args` is a raw CLI escape hatch — non-portable across harnesses |\n115\t| `prompt` | agent input (not config). Never quote signal syntax literally in prompts — describe it (\"emit signal planned\"); the engine delivers the syntax to the agent |\n116\t| `timeout` | per **attempt**, seconds |\n117\t| `max_attempts` | attempts per runner, default 1. Primary gets N, then fallback gets N. Retryable outcomes: non-zero exit, timeout (recorded as rc 124), and **silence** — an agent body exiting 0 with no known signal (the most common agent flake: the work happened, the tag didn't). Silence retries on the **primary only** and never triggers fallback (another model drops the tag just as often; blind fallback duplicates side effects); after all attempts it classifies as `__default__`. Shell silence is deterministic and is not retried. **Silence handling is decision-node behavior**: in pools the body is not expected to signal — silence at rc 0 is the normal ok outcome (see the pool rows) |\n118\t| `fallback` | alternate agent action after primary attempts are exhausted. Agent-only (a fallback for shell is meaningless); a fallback has no fallback |\n119\t| `ignore_exit_code` | rc != 0 doesn't classify the body as failed; outcome comes from signals. **Forbidden in pool nodes** — `min_success` already owns that role |\n120\t\n121\tHooks around the body — `pre` / `post` (shell-only; rendered like everything else). These are not lifecycle hooks but **deterministic voices in the signal channel** — the only way to put shell before/after an agent body (you can't append a line to a prompt):\n122\t\n123\t| `pre` — once per node run, before the body renders | Effect |\n124\t|---|---|\n125\t| emits a routing signal | body and `post` are **skipped**, the signal routes (guard: \"already done / not needed\") |\n126\t| emits `var` | applied **before** the body renders — env prep, the prompt sees fresh vars |\n127\t| exits non-zero | `__failed__` (preparation broke), body never runs |\n128\t| exits 0, silent | normal path |\n129\t\n130\t| `post` — after **every** attempt, before signal resolution; sees `MEDULLA_BODY_RC` / `MEDULLA_BODY_SIGNAL` | Effect |\n131\t|---|---|\n132\t| exits non-zero | the **attempt failed** → body+post retry within `max_attempts`, then fallback (\"try until the artifact exists\": `post: test -s out.md`) |\n133\t| exits 0 + emits a signal | **overrides** the body's signal (the agent said planned, the plan is garbage → route needs_rework) |\n134\t| exits 0, silent | the body's outcome stands |\n135\t\n136\tIn pools both run per input: a `pre` guard skips already-done inputs (manifest `ok: true` with the guard's signal); a `post` check is the truth channel for agent inputs — CLIs exit 0 even when the model did nothing, so without `post` a pool's `min_success` counts air.\n137\t\n138\tPool (presence of `inputs` turns the action into a pool):\n139\t\n140\t| Field | Meaning |\n141\t|---|---|\n142\t| `inputs` | YAML list = **data** (scalars or objects, one kind per pool, arrays forbidden), or `{shell: \"cmd\", timeout: 60}` = **source**. Output sniffing by first byte: `[` JSON array, `{` JSON-lines, else plain lines. A bare string is a hard validation error (data vs code ambiguity). Hard cap: 10 000 inputs |\n143\t| `max_parallel` | pool cap: `1` (default, sequential) \\| N \\| `all` |\n144\t| `min_success` | join threshold: `all` (default) \\| N ≥ 1. Input ok = rc == 0. No short-circuiting ever — all inputs run (side effects have value) |\n145\t\n146\tRouting:\n147\t\n148\t| Field | Meaning |\n149\t|---|---|\n150\t| `on_signal` | map of signal → target. Targets are plain strings: a node name, `__exit_ok__`, `__exit_fail__` |\n151\t\n152\t### The reserved namespace — all 8 names\n153\t\n154\tLeft-side law: **a bare name is a signal your code emits; a dunder is an engine key.** Right-side law: **terminals are `__exit_*`.**\n155\t\n156\tRouting signals (left side):\n157\t\n158\t| Name | Emitted by | When | Built-in route |\n159\t|---|---|---|---|\n160\t| `__done__` | pool join | successes ≥ `min_success` | **none — must be routed explicitly** (it's a real edge) |\n161\t| `__failed__` | engine | decision node: body died after all attempts+fallback. Pool: join below threshold | `__exit_fail__` |\n162\t| `__empty__` | engine | source returned rc 0 and zero inputs (bodies never run) | `__exit_fail__` — loud by default; route explicitly where emptiness is legal |\n163\t| `__default__` | nobody (matcher) | body exited rc 0 with no known signal (\"said nothing\") | `__exit_fail__` |\n164\t\n165\tChannel signals (emitted in stdout, never route; reserved bare words — using them as `on_signal` keys is a validation error):\n166\t\n167\t| Name | Meaning |\n168\t|---|---|\n169\t| `var` | `<signal:var key=K>value</signal:var>` — set a variable (applied per the fold law) |\n170\t| `update` | `<signal:update>msg</signal:update>` — progress message |\n171\t\n172\tTerminal nodes (right side):\n173\t\n174\t| Name | Action |\n175\t|---|---|\n176\t| `__exit_ok__` | end the run, exit 0 |\n177\t| `__exit_fail__` | end the run, exit 2; the routing signal's body becomes the error message |\n178\t\n179\tSignals are read from **stdout only**; stderr goes verbatim to the attempt log (a traceback that happens to echo signal text must never route the graph). A known signal emitted before a non-zero exit wins over the exit code. Pool bodies' signals never route — they are recorded in the manifest (law of layers: inputs produce data, joins produce transitions). Bare `done`/`failed` on decision nodes are ordinary user signals with no special meaning. User nodes may not be named `__*__` or `on/off/yes/no/true/false` (YAML 1.1 boolean traps).\n180\t\n181\t### Templates & environment\n182\t\n183\t| Template | Meaning |\n184\t|---|---|\n185\t| `{{var:KEY}}`, `{{var:KEY:-default}}` | variable, with optional default |\n186\t| `{{file:path}}` | file inclusion, recursive (depth ≤ 10, exceeding = render error with the inclusion chain; missing file = error). Relative paths resolve against the **including file's** directory. Paths are static — no vars inside |\n187\t| `{{input}}` | the input; objects render as compact JSON |\n188\t| `{{input.a.b:-default}}` | dot-walk into object inputs. Missing field without a default = hard render error |\n189\t| `{{input_index}}` (1-based), `{{input_count}}` | position / total |\n190\t| `{{last.node}}`, `{{last.signal}}`, `{{last.message}}`, `{{last.rc}}` | outcome of the previously completed node — transient tokens (not vars: no persistence, no fold-law constraints). The bridge for agent-bodied handlers whose prompts can't read env |\n191\t\n192\tRender model: phase 1 — file inclusion; phase 2 — one simultaneous, **inert** pass of var/input substitution. **Files are code, values are data**: mustache inside included files resolves fully; mustache inside var/input *values* stays literal (injection-safe by construction). Every scalar field of an action is a template (that's why an ensemble is just a pool with per-input `harness`/`model`). A field rendering to an empty string counts as absent — for optional agent fields only; empty `shell`/`prompt`/`harness` is an error. Rendering happens **once per node run**, before attempt 1; retries reuse the same rendered text. A render error on a decision node (phantom input) is an engine crash (`E_RENDER`) — the template itself is broken. A render error for **one pool input** fails that input only (manifest row `reason: render` with the template path and input index) — one malformed row of producer data must not kill the other inputs.\n193\t\n194\tEnvironment (data should flow to shell via env, templates are for slugs/paths — quoting-safe):\n195\t\n196\t| Variable | Meaning |\n197\t|---|---|\n198\t| `MEDULLA_INPUT` | the input as JSON |\n199\t| `MEDULLA_INPUT_INDEX` / `MEDULLA_INPUT_COUNT` | position / total |\n200\t| `MEDULLA_INPUT_<KEY>` | each flat scalar field of an object input, uppercased |\n201\t| `MEDULLA_INPUT_KEY` / `MEDULLA_ATTEMPT_ID` | stable input identity `(index, hash)` / unique attempt id — the idempotency keys for bodies that mutate the outside world (branches, PRs, tickets) |\n202\t| `MEDULLA_LAST_NODE` / `_SIGNAL` / `_MESSAGE` / `_RC` | outcome of the previously completed node, published before every transition (after a pool, `_RC` is empty — a join has no single rc; read the manifest); `MEDULLA_LAST_EVENT_JSON` carries the same as one JSON object. Timeout is recognizable as rc 124 |\n203\t| `MEDULLA_MANIFEST_<NODE>` | path to a pool node's manifest (dashes → underscores) |\n204\t| `MEDULLA_RUN_ID` / `MEDULLA_RUN_DIR` | run id (settable from outside for correlation; else generated) / this run's directory. Put artifacts in `$MEDULLA_RUN_DIR/artifacts/` |\n205\t| `MEDULLA_TIMEOUT_S` | resolved step timeout, for CLIs that need to size their own |\n206\t\n207\tAll pipeline vars are exported to child processes. Reserved names (`PATH`, `HOME`, `SHELL`, `LD_*`, …) are rejected by the validator.\n208\t\n209\tVar-signal semantics (fold law): variables are mutable state, and state mutation requires ordering — var signals are **applied only at `max_parallel: 1`** (which includes every decision node), in input order, atomically from the **successful** attempt only. At `max_parallel > 1` they are recorded in the manifest instead.\n210\t\n211\t### Errors & exit codes\n212\t\n213\tTwo failure classes. The test: *can it be fixed by changing data/prompts/retrying?* → workflow failure, the graph decides. *Does it require editing the pipeline/environment?* → engine crash.\n214\t\n215\t| Exit | Class | Meaning |\n216\t|---|---|---|\n217\t| 0 | — | `__exit_ok__` |\n218\t| 1 | engine crash | the pipeline itself is broken — fix the pipeline, retrying is pointless |\n219\t| 2 | workflow failure | the graph routed to `__exit_fail__` — fix the task/inputs |\n220\t| 130 | interrupt | — |\n221\t\n222\tA fixed delay separates attempts and the fallback switch (`MEDULLA_RETRY_DELAY_S`, default 2s — retry storms hit provider rate limits).\n223\t\n224\tCrash codes: `E_VALIDATION` (schema/XOR/unknown target/boolean node names/bare keys in pool routing/defaults-inherited self-edges), `E_RENDER` (broken decision-node template: missing file, depth > 10, empty required render), `E_DEADLINE` (pipeline timeout), `E_INPUTS` (source exited non-zero, or emitted mixed-kind/array elements — a broken producer is not an empty queue), `E_INPUTS_LIMIT` (> 10k), `E_HARNESS`, `E_INTERNAL`.\n225\t\n226\t`E_HARNESS` is razor-thin by design: **only** \"harness binary missing / unresolvable\". An agent process dying unexpectedly (OOM, segfault, API hiccup) is always a non-zero exit — class B, retryable. If that boundary drifts, transient flakes start crashing whole runs.\n227\t\n228\t#### Handling errors in the graph\n229\t\n230\tHandlers are **ordinary nodes routed before the terminal** — never a body on the terminal (`kill -9` makes exit hooks an illusion; a node has a timeout, attempts and its own log). The error payload arrives through the same channels as all data: `$MEDULLA_LAST_*` for shell, `{{last.*}}` for prompts. Global catch-all is three lines of `defaults`:\n231\t\n232\t```yaml\n233\tdefaults:\n234\t  on_signal: {__failed__: notify, __default__: notify}   # root supervisor\n235\t\n236\tnodes:\n237\t  notify:\n238\t    shell: 'curl -s \"$HOOK\" -d \"text=[medulla] $MEDULLA_LAST_NODE ($MEDULLA_LAST_SIGNAL): $MEDULLA_LAST_MESSAGE\"'\n239\t    timeout: 30\n240\t    on_signal: {__default__: __exit_fail__, __failed__: __exit_fail__}   # own dunders explicit!\n241\t```\n242\t\n243\tA node-level edge beats the defaults catch-all, which beats built-ins — a three-tier supervision chain. The validator rejects a defaults-inherited edge that points at its own node (`notify` failing into `notify` would loop); explicit self-loops remain legal (retry pattern). A pool's `__failed__` message is pre-aggregated: `\"2/5 inputs ok (min_success=3); rc!=0 x2, timeout x1, render x0\"` — the manifest has the rest. Class A is not catchable in the graph by definition: the graph itself is what's broken.\n244\t\n245\tThe error **message is the body of the signal** that routed to `__exit_fail__` (engine facts carry their own: `__failed__` → rc/join stats, `__empty__` → \"source returned 0 inputs\", `__default__` → tail of stdout). Every run ends with an atomic `outcome.json`:\n246\t\n247\t```json\n248\t{\"outcome\": \"failed\", \"exit_code\": 2,\n249\t \"error\": {\"code\": \"SIGNAL_FAIL\", \"message\": \"no repo access: git clone rc=128\",\n250\t           \"node\": \"plan\", \"step\": 12, \"signal\": \"blocked\"},\n251\t \"steps\": 12, \"duration_s\": 4180}\n252\t```\n253\t\n254\t### Lifecycle\n255\t\n256\t**Boot** — parse CLI → load yaml (`version: \"2\"` or a friendly migration error) → validate everything (`E_VALIDATION` before any run dir exists) → create `runs/<ts>-<run_id>/`, snapshot the config, seed vars, prune old runs → set the deadline.\n257\t\n258\t**Node loop** (single program counter) — per node: deadline check → materialize inputs (no key → phantom; list → snapshot into the step dir; source → render, execute, sniff, check) → run the pool (`max_parallel` workers; per input: render once → attempts → fallback; stream stdout to the step log with realtime signal extraction) → classify (decision: signal | `__failed__` | `__default__`; pool: `__done__` | `__failed__` | `__empty__`) → resolve the edge (node `on_signal` → `defaults.on_signal` → built-ins) → append the journal row → next node or terminal.\n259\t\n260\t**Finish** — atomic `outcome.json`, exit 0/2; crashes write `outcome.json` with the `E_*` code and exit 1; SIGINT → best-effort outcome, exit 130.\n261\t\n262\t**Resume** — pick the latest run without `outcome.json`, or with `outcome: interrupted` **or `crashed`** (deliberate extension: the #1 resume trigger is the `E_DEADLINE` crash; config-class crashes simply crash again identically) — or `--run <dir>`: reload the **snapshot** config (a run's config is immutable), vars, journal position; an interrupted pool continues from the manifest done-mask (input identity = `(index, hash)`; sources are never re-executed on resume); an interrupted decision node re-runs whole (body idempotence is the author's concern). The deadline is fresh per invocation.\n263\t\n264\t### Layout\n265\t\n266\tA pipeline is a self-contained directory — contract, code, history:\n267\t\n268\t```\n269\t.medulla/pipelines/<name>/\n270\t  pipeline.yaml            # the contract\n271\t  prompts/  scripts/       # its code\n272\t  harness/                 # phase 2: harness HOME (sessions), shared by all runs\n273\t  runs/<ts>-<run_id>/      # one directory per run\n274\t    pipeline.yaml          # config snapshot as loaded (immutable for the run)\n275\t    journal.jsonl          # graph chronology, append-only (step, node, rc, signal, message, duration)\n276\t    vars.yaml              # variables (updated on var signals)\n277\t    outcome.json           # written only on completion (atomic); absent = running or hard-killed\n278\t    steps/\n279\t      001-triage/                        # every step gets a directory\n280\t      002-plan/prompt.md                 # rendered agent input (what the agent actually saw)\n281\t      002-plan/attempt-1-codex.txt       # raw CLI stream per attempt\n282\t      004-apply/inputs.json              # inputs snapshot (resume)\n283\t      004-apply/input-2-sonnet.txt       # per-input logs\n284\t      004-apply/manifest.jsonl           # {index, key, input, ok, reason, signal, message,\n285\t                                         #  rc, timed_out, attempts, fallback, harness, model,\n286\t                                         #  vars, updates, duration_s, log}\n287\t```\n288\t\n289\tRetention: on start, keep the newest `keep_runs` finished runs; directories without `outcome.json` younger than the pipeline timeout are never pruned. History browsing needs no CLI: `ls runs/`, `cat outcome.json`.\n290\t\n291\t**Phase 2 (designed, not in phase 1):** pipeline-scoped harness sessions — `harness/` as the container HOME, session ids captured into journal/manifest from the CLI streams the engine already parses, and a `resume:` field on the agent block to continue a node's last successful session (current run first, then previous runs, newest first). Docker: everything lives under `/workspace` (already mounted RW); credentials are copied once from the read-only `/mnt/*` mounts.\n292\t\n293\t### Canonical patterns\n294\t\n295\t- **Budget gate** (bounded rework — the engine has no per-node visit caps; cycle semantics belong to the workflow):\n296\t  ```yaml\n297\t  gate:\n298\t    shell: |\n299\t      n=$(( ${PLAN_TRIES:-0} + 1 ))\n300\t      echo \"<signal:var key=PLAN_TRIES>$n</signal:var>\"\n301\t      [ \"$n\" -le 3 ] && echo \"<signal:go>ok</signal:go>\" || echo \"<signal:budget_out>ok</signal:budget_out>\"\n302\t    on_signal: {go: plan, budget_out: escalate}\n303\t  ```\n304\t- **Crawler**: producer node → pool → probe node → edge back; the source re-runs on each new node run.\n305\t- **Heterogeneous pool**: inputs carry `role`/`prompt` fields; the node prompt is the template (code, vars resolve), input fragments are inserted inert.\n306\t- **Entry cleanup** (crash-only): there is no `finally`; exit hooks are an illusion under `kill -9`. Clean stale state idempotently at the start of the node/run that needs it clean.\n307\t- **Parallel tickets**: the engine guarantees vars isolation; file/git isolation is the body's job (`git worktree` per input) and disjointness is the producer script's contract.\n308\t- **DLQ (repair node)**: failed pool inputs are structured data — re-enqueue only them, never the whole pool:\n309\t  ```yaml\n310\t  retry-failed:\n311\t    inputs: {shell: \"jq -c 'select(.ok|not) | .input' $MEDULLA_MANIFEST_APPLY\"}\n312\t    max_parallel: 2\n313\t    shell: 'bash scripts/fix_one.sh \"$MEDULLA_INPUT_ID\"'\n314\t    on_signal: {__done__: report, __empty__: report}\n315\t  ```\n316\t\n317\t### Migrating from v1\n318\t\n319\tThe v1 engine is removed; this table is the dictionary for porting old pipelines.\n320\t\n321\t| v1 | v2 |\n322\t|---|---|\n323\t| `stages` / `starting` | `nodes` / `start` |\n324\t| `runner:` / `llm:` / `executor`+`command` | action fields directly on the node: `agent: {harness, model, effort, args}` xor `shell` |\n325\t| `loop:` + `list:` + `fetch:` + `parallel: true` | `inputs:` on the node + `max_parallel` |\n326\t| `done: __next_item__` + `loop_done` | pool joins route `__done__` / `__failed__` / `__empty__` via `min_success` |\n327\t| `max_iterations` / `reset_iterations` / `on_max` | removed — budget gate pattern (vars) |\n328\t| hardcoded `max_rounds=500` | pipeline `timeout` (wall-clock deadline) |\n329\t| `round_timeout` / `fallback_runner` | `defaults: {timeout, fallback}` |\n330\t| `__exit__` | `__exit_ok__` / `__exit_fail__` |\n331\t| `ignore_rc` | `ignore_exit_code` (decision nodes only) |\n332\t| `{{__item__}}` / `{{__list_item__}}` | `{{input}}` family + `MEDULLA_INPUT_*` env |\n333\t| `MEDULLA_TASK_ID` | `MEDULLA_RUN_ID` |\n334\t| `.medulla/vars.<task>.yaml` | `.medulla/pipelines/<name>/runs/<id>/` |\n335\t| `--stage` | `--node` |\n336\t| gemini executor | removed (use `agy`) |\n337\t| exit codes 0/1/2/3 ad-hoc | 0 = ok, 1 = engine crash, 2 = workflow fail, 130 = interrupt |\n338\t\n339\t### Reserved (designed, not implemented — in priority order)\n340\t\n341\t`stall_timeout` (no-stdout watchdog for hung agents; partially covered today by per-harness flags — codex `stream_idle_timeout_ms`, agy `--print-timeout`) · manifest attempt states (`claimed|started|completed`) + per-node resume policy `rerun|skip|probe` (exactly-once is impossible; make duplicate side effects detectable) · `resume:` (continue a node's session — phase 2) · `cancel_rest` (race joins) · `on_input_fail: abort` (fail-fast pools) · `format:` on sources (override sniffing) · `finally` (best-effort only, if reality ever demands it) · agent-block defaults.\n342\t"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"31358358-0e02-4f11-9160-c99122fc9ba8","uuid":"82a66dee-cdc1-46dd-85da-d7c2ba2b45bb","timestamp":"2026-07-15T11:04:01.634Z","tool_use_result":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/Users/ako/Work/ai/pilot-wip/medulla/README.md","content":"# medulla\n\n**medulla is a state machine for AI agents.** You describe work as a YAML pipeline — a graph of **nodes** — and medulla runs each node's action on a shell command or an agent harness (`claude-code`, `codex`, `opencode`, `agy`). Bodies emit **signals**; signals route the graph. Built in: retries, fallback to another model, pools with a success threshold, and crash-safe resume.\n\n```\nnode  = action (shell | agent) [× inputs] → signals → next node\ngraph = nodes + on_signal edges + two terminals (__exit_ok__ / __exit_fail__)\n```\n\n**One machine.** Internally every node is a pool: a node without `inputs:` runs over a single phantom input. Policy (timeouts, attempts, fallback) works identically in both modes. The only thing `inputs:` switches is the **signal contract**: without inputs the body talks to the graph (decision node); with inputs the body writes to the manifest and only the join result routes (pool node).\n\n> **Status**: v2 contract (frozen), engine implemented — the v1 engine is **deleted**; v1 pipelines are not supported. `version: \"2\"` is required in every pipeline; the engine rejects anything else with a pointer to the migration table below. Implementation phases: **1** — engine (this document), **2** — harness sessions & run history polish.\n\n## Usage\n\n```bash\nmedulla -w .medulla/pipelines/<name>              # run a pipeline\nmedulla -w ... --var KEY=VALUE                    # set/override vars\nmedulla -w ... --node <name>                      # dev: start from a specific node\nmedulla -w ... --resume                           # continue the latest unfinished run\nmedulla -w ... --run <dir>                        # continue a specific run\nmedulla --docker -w ...                           # run inside the pipeline's Docker image\n```\n\n## Example\n\n```yaml\nversion: \"2\"\nstart: triage\ntimeout: 86400                # whole-run deadline (default 24h; 0 = unlimited)\nvars: {BRANCH: main}\n\ndefaults:                     # policy defaults for every action (\"field absent → take from here\")\n  timeout: 1800\n  fallback: {agent: {harness: claude-code, model: opus}}\n\nnodes:\n\n  # decision node: body signals route the graph\n  triage:\n    shell: |\n      git worktree prune; rm -f .locks/*        # crash-only: clean up on entry\n      n=$(rg -l \"FIXME\" src/ | wc -l | tr -d ' ')\n      [ \"$n\" -gt 0 ] && echo \"<signal:found>ok</signal:found>\" || echo \"<signal:clean>ok</signal:clean>\"\n    timeout: 60\n    on_signal: {found: plan, clean: __exit_ok__}\n\n  plan:\n    agent: {harness: codex, model: gpt-5.5, effort: xhigh}\n    prompt: |\n      {{file:prompts/plan.md}}\n      Branch: {{var:BRANCH}}. Write the plan to plan.md and emit signal planned.\n    max_attempts: 2\n    fallback: {agent: {harness: claude-code, model: sonnet}}\n    on_signal:\n      planned: panel\n      __failed__: __exit_fail__    # body died (rc != 0 after attempts+fallback)\n\n  # pool node: inputs switch the contract — the join routes, bodies write to the manifest\n  panel:\n    inputs:\n      - {slug: gpt5,   harness: codex,       model: gpt-5.5, effort: xhigh}\n      - {slug: sonnet, harness: claude-code, model: sonnet}\n      - {slug: gem,    harness: agy,         model: \"Gemini 3.1 Pro (High)\"}\n    max_parallel: all\n    min_success: 1\n    agent: {harness: \"{{input.harness}}\", model: \"{{input.model}}\", effort: \"{{input.effort:-}}\"}\n    prompt: |\n      You are panelist {{input.slug}} ({{input_index}}/{{input_count}}).\n      Critique the plan: {{file:plan.md}}\n      Write your verdict to reviews/{{input.slug}}.md\n    post: 'test -s \"reviews/{{input.slug}}.md\"'   # verdict = artifact exists, not agent mood\n    on_signal: {__done__: apply}\n\n  apply:\n    inputs: {shell: \"python3 scripts/tickets.py --json\", timeout: 60}\n    max_parallel: 3\n    min_success: 2\n    shell: |\n      bash scripts/fix_one.sh \"$MEDULLA_INPUT_ID\" \"$MEDULLA_INPUT_TITLE\"\n    max_attempts: 2\n    on_signal:\n      __done__: report\n      __empty__: report        # empty queue is legal here — route it explicitly\n\n  report:\n    shell: |\n      ok=$(jq -s 'map(select(.ok))|length' \"$MEDULLA_MANIFEST_APPLY\")\n      total=$(jq -s length \"$MEDULLA_MANIFEST_APPLY\")\n      [ \"$ok\" -eq \"$total\" ] && echo \"<signal:ready>ok</signal:ready>\" || echo \"<signal:rework>ok</signal:rework>\"\n    on_signal: {ready: __exit_ok__, rework: plan}\n```\n\n## Reference\n\n### Pipeline level\n\n| Field | Default | Meaning |\n|---|---|---|\n| `version` | required | must be `\"2\"` |\n| `start` | required | first node |\n| `vars` | `{}` | initial variables (also exported to env; see blacklist below) |\n| `timeout` | 86400 | wall-clock deadline for the whole run; `0` = unlimited. The engine clamps every child timeout to the remaining budget |\n| `defaults` | — | policy defaults for actions: `timeout`, `max_attempts`, `ignore_exit_code`, `fallback`, `on_signal` (per-key merge). Flat scalars only — never merged deep |\n| `keep_runs` | 20 | auto-prune of run history on start |\n\n### Node = action [+ pool] + routing\n\nAction (exactly one of `shell` / `agent`):\n\n| Field | Meaning |\n|---|---|\n| `shell` | shell command; its config *is* the command. `prompt` here is a validation error |\n| `agent` | `{harness, model, effort, args}` — one entity, one block. Scalar shortcut: `agent: codex` ≡ `agent: {harness: codex}`. `args` is a raw CLI escape hatch — non-portable across harnesses |\n| `prompt` | agent input (not config). Never quote signal syntax literally in prompts — describe it (\"emit signal planned\"); the engine delivers the syntax to the agent |\n| `timeout` | per **attempt**, seconds |\n| `max_attempts` | attempts per runner, default 1. Primary gets N, then fallback gets N. Retryable outcomes: non-zero exit, timeout (recorded as rc 124), and **silence** — an agent body exiting 0 with no known signal (the most common agent flake: the work happened, the tag didn't). Silence retries on the **primary only** and never triggers fallback (another model drops the tag just as often; blind fallback duplicates side effects); after all attempts it classifies as `__default__`. Shell silence is deterministic and is not retried. **Silence handling is decision-node behavior**: in pools the body is not expected to signal — silence at rc 0 is the normal ok outcome (see the pool rows) |\n| `fallback` | alternate agent action after primary attempts are exhausted. Agent-only (a fallback for shell is meaningless); a fallback has no fallback |\n| `ignore_exit_code` | rc != 0 doesn't classify the body as failed; outcome comes from signals. **Forbidden in pool nodes** — `min_success` already owns that role |\n\nHooks around the body — `pre` / `post` (shell-only; rendered like everything else). These are not lifecycle hooks but **deterministic voices in the signal channel** — the only way to put shell before/after an agent body (you can't append a line to a prompt):\n\n| `pre` — once per node run, before the body renders | Effect |\n|---|---|\n| emits a routing signal | body and `post` are **skipped**, the signal routes (guard: \"already done / not needed\") |\n| emits `var` | applied **before** the body renders — env prep, the prompt sees fresh vars |\n| exits non-zero | `__failed__` (preparation broke), body never runs |\n| exits 0, silent | normal path |\n\n| `post` — after **every** attempt, before signal resolution; sees `MEDULLA_BODY_RC` / `MEDULLA_BODY_SIGNAL` | Effect |\n|---|---|\n| exits non-zero | the **attempt failed** → body+post retry within `max_attempts`, then fallback (\"try until the artifact exists\": `post: test -s out.md`) |\n| exits 0 + emits a signal | **overrides** the body's signal (the agent said planned, the plan is garbage → route needs_rework) |\n| exits 0, silent | the body's outcome stands |\n\nIn pools both run per input: a `pre` guard skips already-done inputs (manifest `ok: true` with the guard's signal); a `post` check is the truth channel for agent inputs — CLIs exit 0 even when the model did nothing, so without `post` a pool's `min_success` counts air.\n\nPool (presence of `inputs` turns the action into a pool):\n\n| Field | Meaning |\n|---|---|\n| `inputs` | YAML list = **data** (scalars or objects, one kind per pool, arrays forbidden), or `{shell: \"cmd\", timeout: 60}` = **source**. Output sniffing by first byte: `[` JSON array, `{` JSON-lines, else plain lines. A bare string is a hard validation error (data vs code ambiguity). Hard cap: 10 000 inputs |\n| `max_parallel` | pool cap: `1` (default, sequential) \\| N \\| `all` |\n| `min_success` | join threshold: `all` (default) \\| N ≥ 1. Input ok = rc == 0. No short-circuiting ever — all inputs run (side effects have value) |\n\nRouting:\n\n| Field | Meaning |\n|---|---|\n| `on_signal` | map of signal → target. Targets are plain strings: a node name, `__exit_ok__`, `__exit_fail__` |\n\n### The reserved namespace — all 8 names\n\nLeft-side law: **a bare name is a signal your code emits; a dunder is an engine key.** Right-side law: **terminals are `__exit_*`.**\n\nRouting signals (left side):\n\n| Name | Emitted by | When | Built-in route |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| `__done__` | pool join | successes ≥ `min_success` | **none — must be routed explicitly** (it's a real edge) |\n| `__failed__` | engine | decision node: body died after all attempts+fallback. Pool: join below threshold | `__exit_fail__` |\n| `__empty__` | engine | source returned rc 0 and zero inputs (bodies never run) | `__exit_fail__` — loud by default; route explicitly where emptiness is legal |\n| `__default__` | nobody (matcher) | body exited rc 0 with no known signal (\"said nothing\") | `__exit_fail__` |\n\nChannel signals (emitted in stdout, never route; reserved bare words — using them as `on_signal` keys is a validation error):\n\n| Name | Meaning |\n|---|---|\n| `var` | `<signal:var key=K>value</signal:var>` — set a variable (applied per the fold law) |\n| `update` | `<signal:update>msg</signal:update>` — progress message |\n\nTerminal nodes (right side):\n\n| Name | Action |\n|---|---|\n| `__exit_ok__` | end the run, exit 0 |\n| `__exit_fail__` | end the run, exit 2; the routing signal's body becomes the error message |\n\nSignals are read from **stdout only**; stderr goes verbatim to the attempt log (a traceback that happens to echo signal text must never route the graph). A known signal emitted before a non-zero exit wins over the exit code. Pool bodies' signals never route — they are recorded in the manifest (law of layers: inputs produce data, joins produce transitions). Bare `done`/`failed` on decision nodes are ordinary user signals with no special meaning. User nodes may not be named `__*__` or `on/off/yes/no/true/false` (YAML 1.1 boolean traps).\n\n### Templates & environment\n\n| Template | Meaning |\n|---|---|\n| `{{var:KEY}}`, `{{var:KEY:-default}}` | variable, with optional default |\n| `{{file:path}}` | file inclusion, recursive (depth ≤ 10, exceeding = render error with the inclusion chain; missing file = error). Relative paths resolve against the **including file's** directory. Paths are static — no vars inside |\n| `{{input}}` | the input; objects render as compact JSON |\n| `{{input.a.b:-default}}` | dot-walk into object inputs. Missing field without a default = hard render error |\n| `{{input_index}}` (1-based), `{{input_count}}` | position / total |\n| `{{last.node}}`, `{{last.signal}}`, `{{last.message}}`, `{{last.rc}}` | outcome of the previously completed node — transient tokens (not vars: no persistence, no fold-law constraints). The bridge for agent-bodied handlers whose prompts can't read env |\n\nRender model: phase 1 — file inclusion; phase 2 — one simultaneous, **inert** pass of var/input substitution. **Files are code, values are data**: mustache inside included files resolves fully; mustache inside var/input *values* stays literal (injection-safe by construction). Every scalar field of an action is a template (that's why an ensemble is just a pool with per-input `harness`/`model`). A field rendering to an empty string counts as absent — for optional agent fields only; empty `shell`/`prompt`/`harness` is an error. Rendering happens **once per node run**, before attempt 1; retries reuse the same rendered text. A render error on a decision node (phantom input) is an engine crash (`E_RENDER`) — the template itself is broken. A render error for **one pool input** fails that input only (manifest row `reason: render` with the template path and input index) — one malformed row of producer data must not kill the other inputs.\n\nEnvironment (data should flow to shell via env, templates are for slugs/paths — quoting-safe):\n\n| Variable | Meaning |\n|---|---|\n| `MEDULLA_INPUT` | the input as JSON |\n| `MEDULLA_INPUT_INDEX` / `MEDULLA_INPUT_COUNT` | position / total |\n| `MEDULLA_INPUT_<KEY>` | each flat scalar field of an object input, uppercased |\n| `MEDULLA_INPUT_KEY` / `MEDULLA_ATTEMPT_ID` | stable input identity `(index, hash)` / unique attempt id — the idempotency keys for bodies that mutate the outside world (branches, PRs, tickets) |\n| `MEDULLA_LAST_NODE` / `_SIGNAL` / `_MESSAGE` / `_RC` | outcome of the previously completed node, published before every transition (after a pool, `_RC` is empty — a join has no single rc; read the manifest); `MEDULLA_LAST_EVENT_JSON` carries the same as one JSON object. Timeout is recognizable as rc 124 |\n| `MEDULLA_MANIFEST_<NODE>` | path to a pool node's manifest (dashes → underscores) |\n| `MEDULLA_RUN_ID` / `MEDULLA_RUN_DIR` | run id (settable from outside for correlation; else generated) / this run's directory. Put artifacts in `$MEDULLA_RUN_DIR/artifacts/` |\n| `MEDULLA_TIMEOUT_S` | resolved step timeout, for CLIs that need to size their own |\n\nAll pipeline vars are exported to child processes. Reserved names (`PATH`, `HOME`, `SHELL`, `LD_*`, …) are rejected by the validator.\n\nVar-signal semantics (fold law): variables are mutable state, and state mutation requires ordering — var signals are **applied only at `max_parallel: 1`** (which includes every decision node), in input order, atomically from the **successful** attempt only. At `max_parallel > 1` they are recorded in the manifest instead.\n\n### Errors & exit codes\n\nTwo failure classes. The test: *can it be fixed by changing data/prompts/retrying?* → workflow failure, the graph decides. *Does it require editing the pipeline/environment?* → engine crash.\n\n| Exit | Class | Meaning |\n|---|---|---|\n| 0 | — | `__exit_ok__` |\n| 1 | engine crash | the pipeline itself is broken — fix the pipeline, retrying is pointless |\n| 2 | workflow failure | the graph routed to `__exit_fail__` — fix the task/inputs |\n| 130 | interrupt | — |\n\nA fixed delay separates attempts and the fallback switch (`MEDULLA_RETRY_DELAY_S`, default 2s — retry storms hit provider rate limits).\n\nCrash codes: `E_VALIDATION` (schema/XOR/unknown target/boolean node names/bare keys in pool routing/defaults-inherited self-edges), `E_RENDER` (broken decision-node template: missing file, depth > 10, empty required render), `E_DEADLINE` (pipeline timeout), `E_INPUTS` (source exited non-zero, or emitted mixed-kind/array elements — a broken producer is not an empty queue), `E_INPUTS_LIMIT` (> 10k), `E_HARNESS`, `E_INTERNAL`.\n\n`E_HARNESS` is razor-thin by design: **only** \"harness binary missing / unresolvable\". An agent process dying unexpectedly (OOM, segfault, API hiccup) is always a non-zero exit — class B, retryable. If that boundary drifts, transient flakes start crashing whole runs.\n\n#### Handling errors in the graph\n\nHandlers are **ordinary nodes routed before the terminal** — never a body on the terminal (`kill -9` makes exit hooks an illusion; a node has a timeout, attempts and its own log). The error payload arrives through the same channels as all data: `$MEDULLA_LAST_*` for shell, `{{last.*}}` for prompts. Global catch-all is three lines of `defaults`:\n\n```yaml\ndefaults:\n  on_signal: {__failed__: notify, __default__: notify}   # root supervisor\n\nnodes:\n  notify:\n    shell: 'curl -s \"$HOOK\" -d \"text=[medulla] $MEDULLA_LAST_NODE ($MEDULLA_LAST_SIGNAL): $MEDULLA_LAST_MESSAGE\"'\n    timeout: 30\n    on_signal: {__default__: __exit_fail__, __failed__: __exit_fail__}   # own dunders explicit!\n```\n\nA node-level edge beats the defaults catch-all, which beats built-ins — a three-tier supervision chain. The validator rejects a defaults-inherited edge that points at its own node (`notify` failing into `notify` would loop); explicit self-loops remain legal (retry pattern). A pool's `__failed__` message is pre-aggregated: `\"2/5 inputs ok (min_success=3); rc!=0 x2, timeout x1, render x0\"` — the manifest has the rest. Class A is not catchable in the graph by definition: the graph itself is what's broken.\n\nThe error **message is the body of the signal** that routed to `__exit_fail__` (engine facts carry their own: `__failed__` → rc/join stats, `__empty__` → \"source returned 0 inputs\", `__default__` → tail of stdout). Every run ends with an atomic `outcome.json`:\n\n```json\n{\"outcome\": \"failed\", \"exit_code\": 2,\n \"error\": {\"code\": \"SIGNAL_FAIL\", \"message\": \"no repo access: git clone rc=128\",\n           \"node\": \"plan\", \"step\": 12, \"signal\": \"blocked\"},\n \"steps\": 12, \"duration_s\": 4180}\n```\n\n### Lifecycle\n\n**Boot** — parse CLI → load yaml (`version: \"2\"` or a friendly migration error) → validate everything (`E_VALIDATION` before any run dir exists) → create `runs/<ts>-<run_id>/`, snapshot the config, seed vars, prune old runs → set the deadline.\n\n**Node loop** (single program counter) — per node: deadline check → materialize inputs (no key → phantom; list → snapshot into the step dir; source → render, execute, sniff, check) → run the pool (`max_parallel` workers; per input: render once → attempts → fallback; stream stdout to the step log with realtime signal extraction) → classify (decision: signal | `__failed__` | `__default__`; pool: `__done__` | `__failed__` | `__empty__`) → resolve the edge (node `on_signal` → `defaults.on_signal` → built-ins) → append the journal row → next node or terminal.\n\n**Finish** — atomic `outcome.json`, exit 0/2; crashes write `outcome.json` with the `E_*` code and exit 1; SIGINT → best-effort outcome, exit 130.\n\n**Resume** — pick the latest run without `outcome.json`, or with `outcome: interrupted` **or `crashed`** (deliberate extension: the #1 resume trigger is the `E_DEADLINE` crash; config-class crashes simply crash again identically) — or `--run <dir>`: reload the **snapshot** config (a run's config is immutable), vars, journal position; an interrupted pool continues from the manifest done-mask (input identity = `(index, hash)`; sources are never re-executed on resume); an interrupted decision node re-runs whole (body idempotence is the author's concern). The deadline is fresh per invocation.\n\n### Layout\n\nA pipeline is a self-contained directory — contract, code, history:\n\n```\n.medulla/pipelines/<name>/\n  pipeline.yaml            # the contract\n  prompts/  scripts/       # its code\n  harness/                 # phase 2: harness HOME (sessions), shared by all runs\n  runs/<ts>-<run_id>/      # one directory per run\n    pipeline.yaml          # config snapshot as loaded (immutable for the run)\n    journal.jsonl          # graph chronology, append-only (step, node, rc, signal, message, duration)\n    vars.yaml              # variables (updated on var signals)\n    outcome.json           # written only on completion (atomic); absent = running or hard-killed\n    steps/\n      001-triage/                        # every step gets a directory\n      002-plan/prompt.md                 # rendered agent input (what the agent actually saw)\n      002-plan/attempt-1-codex.txt       # raw CLI stream per attempt\n      004-apply/inputs.json              # inputs snapshot (resume)\n      004-apply/input-2-sonnet.txt       # per-input logs\n      004-apply/manifest.jsonl           # {index, key, input, ok, reason, signal, message,\n                                         #  rc, timed_out, attempts, fallback, harness, model,\n                                         #  vars, updates, duration_s, log}\n```\n\nRetention: on start, keep the newest `keep_runs` finished runs; directories without `outcome.json` younger than the pipeline timeout are never pruned. History browsing needs no CLI: `ls runs/`, `cat outcome.json`.\n\n**Phase 2 (designed, not in phase 1):** pipeline-scoped harness sessions — `harness/` as the container HOME, session ids captured into journal/manifest from the CLI streams the engine already parses, and a `resume:` field on the agent block to continue a node's last successful session (current run first, then previous runs, newest first). Docker: everything lives under `/workspace` (already mounted RW); credentials are copied once from the read-only `/mnt/*` mounts.\n\n### Canonical patterns\n\n- **Budget gate** (bounded rework — the engine has no per-node visit caps; cycle semantics belong to the workflow):\n  ```yaml\n  gate:\n    shell: |\n      n=$(( ${PLAN_TRIES:-0} + 1 ))\n      echo \"<signal:var key=PLAN_TRIES>$n</signal:var>\"\n      [ \"$n\" -le 3 ] && echo \"<signal:go>ok</signal:go>\" || echo \"<signal:budget_out>ok</signal:budget_out>\"\n    on_signal: {go: plan, budget_out: escalate}\n  ```\n- **Crawler**: producer node → pool → probe node → edge back; the source re-runs on each new node run.\n- **Heterogeneous pool**: inputs carry `role`/`prompt` fields; the node prompt is the template (code, vars resolve), input fragments are inserted inert.\n- **Entry cleanup** (crash-only): there is no `finally`; exit hooks are an illusion under `kill -9`. Clean stale state idempotently at the start of the node/run that needs it clean.\n- **Parallel tickets**: the engine guarantees vars isolation; file/git isolation is the body's job (`git worktree` per input) and disjointness is the producer script's contract.\n- **DLQ (repair node)**: failed pool inputs are structured data — re-enqueue only them, never the whole pool:\n  ```yaml\n  retry-failed:\n    inputs: {shell: \"jq -c 'select(.ok|not) | .input' $MEDULLA_MANIFEST_APPLY\"}\n    max_parallel: 2\n    shell: 'bash scripts/fix_one.sh \"$MEDULLA_INPUT_ID\"'\n    on_signal: {__done__: report, __empty__: report}\n  ```\n\n### Migrating from v1\n\nThe v1 engine is removed; this table is the dictionary for porting old pipelines.\n\n| v1 | v2 |\n|---|---|\n| `stages` / `starting` | `nodes` / `start` |\n| `runner:` / `llm:` / `executor`+`command` | action fields directly on the node: `agent: {harness, model, effort, args}` xor `shell` |\n| `loop:` + `list:` + `fetch:` + `parallel: true` | `inputs:` on the node + `max_parallel` |\n| `done: __next_item__` + `loop_done` | pool joins route `__done__` / `__failed__` / `__empty__` via `min_success` |\n| `max_iterations` / `reset_iterations` / `on_max` | removed — budget gate pattern (vars) |\n| hardcoded `max_rounds=500` | pipeline `timeout` (wall-clock deadline) |\n| `round_timeout` / `fallback_runner` | `defaults: {timeout, fallback}` |\n| `__exit__` | `__exit_ok__` / `__exit_fail__` |\n| `ignore_rc` | `ignore_exit_code` (decision nodes only) |\n| `{{__item__}}` / `{{__list_item__}}` | `{{input}}` family + `MEDULLA_INPUT_*` env |\n| `MEDULLA_TASK_ID` | `MEDULLA_RUN_ID` |\n| `.medulla/vars.<task>.yaml` | `.medulla/pipelines/<name>/runs/<id>/` |\n| `--stage` | `--node` |\n| gemini executor | removed (use `agy`) |\n| exit codes 0/1/2/3 ad-hoc | 0 = ok, 1 = engine crash, 2 = workflow fail, 130 = interrupt |\n\n### Reserved (designed, not implemented — in priority order)\n\n`stall_timeout` (no-stdout watchdog for hung agents; partially covered today by per-harness flags — codex `stream_idle_timeout_ms`, agy `--print-timeout`) · manifest attempt states (`claimed|started|completed`) + per-node resume policy `rerun|skip|probe` (exactly-once is impossible; make duplicate side effects detectable) · `resume:` (continue a node's session — phase 2) · `cancel_rest` (race joins) · `on_input_fail: abort` (fail-fast pools) · `format:` on sources (override sniffing) · `finally` (best-effort only, if reality ever demands it) · agent-block defaults.\n","numLines":342,"startLine":1,"totalLines":342}}}

── vars (fold law application point) ──\n221\t    @staticmethod\n222\t    def _valid_var_key(key: str) -> bool:\n223\t        return bool(VAR_NAME_RE.match(key)) and key not in ENV_BLACKLIST_EXACT and \\\n224\t            not any(key.startswith(p) for p in ENV_BLACKLIST_PREFIX)\n225\t\n226\t    def _apply_vars(self, pending: dict[str, str]) -> None:\n227\t        if not pending:\n228\t            return\n229\t        for key, value in pending.items():\n230\t            if not self._valid_var_key(key):\n231\t                log(f\"warn: var '{key}' rejected (reserved/invalid name)\")\n232\t                continue\n233\t            self.vars[key] = value\n234\t        self.store.write_vars(self.vars)\n235\t\n236\t    # ── the attempts seam ────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n254\t    # Owns the FULL hook machinery (panel: pre and post live INSIDE the seam so\n255\t    # part-3 pool workers get identical semantics by calling this per input):\n256\t    # (fold law application) ──\n492\t    def _run_decision(self, node: Node, step_dir: Path, step_no: int):\n493\t        known = self._known(node)\n494\t        render_fn = lambda text, what,                   pool_vars: dict[str, str], sequential: bool) -> dict:\n568\t        \"\"\"Execute one input through the seam; returns a manifest row.\n569\t        Never raises for input-level input_dir.mkdir(exist_ok=True)\n573\t        key = f\"{idx}:{_input_hash(value)}\"\n574\t        local_ctx: dict[str, str] = {}\n575\t\n576\t        input_env = {\n577\t            \"MEDULLA_INPUT\":           input_value=value, has_input=True,\n594\t                              input_index=idx, input_count=count, last=self.last)\n595\t            if required and not rendered.strip():\n596\t Engine facts are excluded from `known`\n    upstream: a body printing <signal:__failed__> must never route (namespace law).\n\n    known=None is pool mode: record the first ANY bare user signal (pool routing\n    tables hold only dunders, yet body signals must reach the manifest).\"\"\"\n    res = ScanResult()\n    for name, attrs, body in extract_signals(stdout):\n        if name == \"update\":\n            res.updates.append(body)\n            continue\n        if name == \"var\":\n            key = (attrs or {}).get(\"key\", \"\")\n            if key and body:\n                res.vars[key] = body\n            continue\n        if res.first_known is not None:\n            continue\n        if known is None:\n            if name not in CHANNEL_SIGNALS and not name.startswith(\"__\"):\n                res.first_known, res.first_body = name, body\n        elif name in known:\n            res.first_known, res.first_body = name, body\n    return res\n\n\n@dataclass\nclass AttemptsOutcome:\n    signal: str | None               # user signal | __failed__ | __default__ | None (pool silent ok)\n    message: str\n    attempts: int                    # total executions across phases (0 = pre decided)\n    attempts_primary: int = 0\n    attempts_fallback: int = 0\n    rc: int | None = None\n    timed_out: bool = False\n    fallback_used: bool = False\n    concluding_phase: str | None = None   # \"primary\" | \"fallback\" | None (pre decided)\n    harness: str | None = None            # harness that produced the concluding outcome\n    model: str | None = None\n    guarded: bool = False                 # pre emitted a routing signal; body never ran\n    failure_class: str | None = None      # for __failed__: \"pre\" | \"rc\" | \"timeout\" | \"post\"\n    recorded_signal: str | None = None    # pool: first bare signal seen (data, never outcome)\n    recorded_body: str = \"\"\n    pending_vars: dict[str, str] = field(default_factory=dict)  # fold law: caller applies\n    updates: list[str] = field(default_factory=list)\n\n\nclass Engine:\n    def __init__(self, pipeline: Pipeline, store: RunStore, workdir: Path):\n        self.p = pipeline\n        self.store = store\n        self.workdir = workdir\n        self.vars: dict[str, str] = dict(pipeline.vars)\n        self.last: dict = {}\n        self.deadline: float | None = (\n            time.monotonic() + pipeline.timeout if pipeline.timeout else None\n        )\n        self.steps = 0\n        self.manifests: dict[str, Path] = {}   # node -> manifest path (engine map, not vars)\n\n    # ── deadline ──\n    def _remaining(self) -> float | None:\n        if self.deadline is None:\n            return None\n        return self.deadline - time.monotonic()\n\n    def _check_deadline(self) -> None:\n        rem = self._remaining()\n        if rem is not None and rem <= 0:\n            raise EngineCrash(E_DEADLINE, f\"pipeline timeout ({self.p.timeout}s) exhausted\")\n\n    def _clamp(self, timeout_s: float) -> float:\n        \"\"\"Clamp a child timeout to the remaining budget (clamp, not crash).\"\"\"\n        rem = self._remaining()\n        if rem is None:\n            return float(timeout_s)\n        if rem <= 0:\n            raise EngineCrash(E_DEADLINE, f\"pipeline timeout ({self.p.timeout}s) exhausted\")\n        return min(float(timeout_s), rem)\n\n    # ── env ──\n    def _base_env(self, vars_map: dict[str, str] | None = None) -> dict[str, str]:\n        env = dict(self.vars if vars_map is None else vars_map)\n        env[\"MEDULLA_RUN_ID\"] = self.store.run_id\n        env[\"MEDULLA_RUN_DIR\"] = str(self.store.dir)\n        for node_name, path in self.manifests.items():\n            env[f\"MEDULLA_MANIFEST_{node_name.upper().replace('-', '_')}\"] = str(path)\n        if self.last:\n            env[\"MEDULLA_LAST_NODE\"] = str(self.last.get(\"node\", \"\"))\n            env[\"MEDULLA_LAST_SIGNAL\"] = str(self.last.get(\"signal\", \"\"))\n            env[\"MEDULLA_LAST_MESSAGE\"] = str(self.last.get(\"message\", \"\"))\n            env[\"MEDULLA_LAST_RC\"] = str(self.last.get(\"rc\", \"\"))\n            env[\"MEDULLA_LAST_EVENT_JSON\"] = json.dumps(self.last, ensure_ascii=False)\n        return env\n\n    # ── vars (fold law application point) ──\n    @staticmethod\n    def _valid_var_key(key: str) -> bool:\n        return bool(VAR_NAME_RE.match(key)) and key not in ENV_BLACKLIST_EXACT and \\\n            not any(key.startswith(p) for p in ENV_BLACKLIST_PREFIX)\n\n    def _apply_vars(self, pending: dict[str, str]) -> None:\n        if not pending:\n            return\n        for key, value in pending.items():\n            if not self._valid_var_key(key):\n                log(f\"warn: var '{key}' rejected (reserved/invalid name)\")\n                continue\n            self.vars[key] = value\n        self.store.write_vars(self.vars)\n\n    # ── render helpers ──\n    def _known(self, node: Node) -> set[str]:\n        return self.p.known_signals(node) - set(CHANNEL_SIGNALS) - set(ENGINE_FACTS)\n\n    def _render_or_crash(self, text: str, node: Node, what: str, required: bool = True) -> str:\n        \"\"\"Decision-context render: any breakage is a pipeline bug -> E_RENDER.\n        required=False: an optional field rendering empty counts as absent (contract).\n        Part-3 pools pass their own render_fn with fail-the-input semantics.\"\"\"\n        try:\n            rendered = render(text, self.p.dir, self.vars, last=self.last)\n        except RenderError as exc:\n            raise EngineCrash(E_RENDER, f\"{what}: {exc}\", node=node.name)\n        if required and not rendered.strip():\n            raise EngineCrash(E_RENDER, f\"{what} rendered empty (broken template or empty field)\",\n                              node=node.name)\n        return rendered\n\n    # ── the attempts seam ────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n    # Owns the FULL hook machinery (panel: pre and post live INSIDE the seam so\n    # part-3 pool workers get identical semantics by calling this per input):\n    # max_parallel>1: record to manifest + local ctx), and body/post vars come\n    # back as pending_vars for the caller to apply per the fold law.\n    def _run_attempts(\n        self,\n        node: Node,\n        step_dir: Path,\n        render_fn,\n        apply_pre_vars,\n        attempt_ns: str,\n        known: set[str] | None,\n        env_fn=None,\n        pool_mode: bool = False,\n    ) -> AttemptsOutcome:\n        # Decision nodes\n        # default to self._base_env (pre vars land in self.vars and are picked up on\n        # the next call); part-3 pool workers pass their own (base + input ctx + local\n        # pre-vars overlay) so parallel inputs never touch shared engine state.\n        if env_fn is None:\n            env_fn = self._base_env\n        action = node.action\n\n        pre_updates: list[str] = BEFORE the body renders\n\n        post_rendered = render_fn(node.post, \"post\") if node.post else None\n\n        current = action\n        phase = \"primary\"\n        fallback = own max_attempts inherits the primary's effective budget\n        phase_budget = self.p.action_max_attempts(action)\n\n        invoke, prompt_text, agent_spec = self._prepare_body(\n        last_failure_class: str | None = None\n        while True:\n            attempt += 1\n            total += 1\n            if phase == \"primary\":\n                n_primary += 1\n pool_mode=pool_mode,\n            )\n            if decision.failure_class is not None:\n                last_failure_class = decision.failure_class\n\n            if move.move is Move.RETRY_SAME:\n                log(f\"attempt {attempt_id} failed (rc={result.rc}), retrying\")\n                _retry_delay()      # a zero-delay retry on a 429 is a provider-ban request\n                continue\n \"\n                           f\"stderr: {_tail(result.stderr)}\")\n                if current.kind == \"agent\":\n                    # harness-mined failure detail (codex error/turn.failed lives in\n                    # stdout JSON the signal filter rightly drops)\n                    detail = resolve_harness(agent_spec).extract_error(result.stdout)\n                    if detail:\n                        message += f\"; adapter.build(rendered_spec, prompt_file, full_prompt, timeout_s)\n        return invoke, prompt_text, rendered_spec\n\n    # ── decision node: the seam + decision-node policy (fold law application) ──\n    def _run_decision(self, node: Node, step_dir: Path, step_no: int):\n        known = self._known(node)\n        render_fn = lambda text, what, required=True: self._render_or_crash(\n            text, node, what, required)\n        outcome = self._run_attempts(\n            node, step_dir, render_fn,\n            apply_pre_vars=self._apply_vars,    # decision = max_parallel 1: vars apply live\n            attempt_ns=f\"{step_no:03d}\", known=known,\n        )\n        if outcome.timed_out and (rem := self._remaining()) is not None and rem <= 0:\n            # killed by the exhausted RUN budget, not its own timeout: a __failed__\n            # here would be exit 2 (not resumable) — this is E_DEADLINE, same law\n            # as deadline-killed pool inputs\n            raise u in outcome.updates:\n            log(f\"update: {u}\")\n        self._apply_vars(outcome.pending_vars)  # body/post vars: routed outcome only\n        return outcome.signal, outcome.message, {\n outcome.model,\n        }\n\n    # ── pool machinery ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\n    def _materialize_inputs(self, node: Node, step_dir: Path) -> list:\n        \"\"\"Snapshot inputs into steps/NNN-<node>/inputs.json (resume foundation).\n        An existing snapshot short-circuits everything: sources are NEVER\n        re-executed on resume (contract), and sequential: bool) -> dict:\n        \"\"\"Execute one input through the seam; returns a manifest row.\n        Never raises for input-level failures; deadline crashes propagate.\"\"\"\n        t0 = time.monotonic()\n        input_dir = step_dir / f\"input-{idx:04d}\"     # per-input namespace: no file races\n        input_dir.mkdir(exist_ok=True)\n        key = f\"{idx}:{_input_hash(value)}\"\n        local_ctx: dict[str, str] = {}\n\n        input_env = {\n            \"MEDULLA_INPUT\": value if isinstance(value, str) else json.dumps(value, ensure_ascii=False),\n            \"MEDULLA_INPUT_INDEX\": str(idx),\n            \"MEDULLA_INPUT_COUNT\": str(count),\n            \"MEDULLA_INPUT_KEY\": key,\n        }\n        if isinstance(value, dict):\n            for k, v in value.items():\n                if isinstance(v, (str, int, float, bool)) and VAR_NAME_RE.match(str(k)):\n                    suffix = str(k).upper()\n                    if suffix not in (\"INDEX\",                             input_value=value, has_input=True,\n                              input_index=idx, input_count=count, last=self.last)\n            if required and not rendered.strip():\n                raise RenderError(f\"{what} rendered empty\")\n            return rendered\n\n        def env_fn() -> dict[str, str]:\n            base = self._base_env(None if sequential else {**pool_vars, **local_ctx})\n            return {**base, **input_env}\n\n        def apply_pre_vars(pending: dict[str, str]) -> None:\n            if sequential:\n                self._apply_vars(pending)             # fold: ordered, not transactional\n            else:\n                # same blacklist as the sequential path — a parallel pre emitting\n                # worker_start)\n            self.display.ensemble_runner_done(\n                source,\n                run_result.exit_code,\n                elapsed,\n                len(run_result.signals or []),\n            )\n            return source, run_result\n\n        if stage.parallel and len(descriptors) > 1:\n            with ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=len(descriptors)) as pool:\n                futures = [pool.submit(worker, r, slug) for r, slug in descriptors]\n                for fut in as_completed(futures):\n                    src, res = fut.result()\n                    results[src] = res\n        else:\n            for r, slug in descriptors:\n                src, res = worker(r, slug)\n                results[src] = res\n\n        successes = sum(1 for r in results.values() if r.exit_code == 0)\n        failures = len(runners) - successes\n\n        threshold = stage.min_success or len(runners)\n        round_ok = successes >= threshold\n\n        return ExecutorResult(\n            output=\"\",\n            exit_code=0 if round_ok else 1,\n            error=(\n                None if round_ok\n                else f\"{failures}/{len(runners)} runner(s) failed; \"\n                     f\"need >= {threshold} success\"\n            ),\n            signals=list(self._live_signals),\n        )\n\n    def _get_raw_prompt(self, stage: Stage) -> str:\n        \"\"\"Return the unresolved prompt (or shell command) for a stage.\n\n        Resolution is deferred to per-runner time so runner.vars overrides\n        compose correctly.\n        \"\"\"\n        if stage.is_ensemble:\n            return stage.prompt or \"\"\n        if stage.runner is not None and stage.runner.executor == \"shell\":\n            return stage.runner.command or \"\"\n        return stage.prompt or \"\"\n\n    def _on_signal(self, sig: Signal) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Real-time callback from executors — display and collect signals.\"\"\"\n        self._live_signals.append(sig)\n        source = sig.attrs.get(\"source\")\n        if self._handle_var_signal(sig, source=source):\n            return\n        if sig.name == \"update\":\n            self.display.update(rich_escape(sig.content), source=source)\n        else:\n            self.display.domain_signal(\n                sig.name, rich_escape(sig.content), source=source,\n            )\n\n    def _run_step(self, label: str, raw_command: str,\n                  show_output: bool = False) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"Run a shell command. Returns True on success.\n\n        Stdout is scanned for `<signal:var key=NAME>VALUE</signal:var>`\n        tags so pre/post hooks can publish vars using the same protocol\n        agents use. Vars are applied to both the vars file and os.environ\n        immediately so the same round's executor can see them.\n\n        show_output: True for pipeline hooks (always visible),\n                     False for stage pre/post steps (verbose only).\n        \"\"\"\n        try:\n            command = resolve_templates(raw_command, self.config_dir, self.vars_path)\n        except TemplateError as e:\n            self.display.warn(f\"{label} template error: {e}\")\n            return False\n\n        self.display.info(f\"[dim]{label}[/]\")\n        proc = subprocess.run(\n            command,\n            shell=True,\n            executable=\"bash\",\n            cwd=self.config_dir,\n            capture_output=True,\n            text=True,\n        )\n\n        if proc.stdout:\n            for sig in parse_signals(proc.stdout):\n                self._handle_var_signal(sig)\n\n            for line in proc.stdout.strip().splitlines():\n                if show_output:\n                    self.display.info(f\"  [dim]{line}[/]\")\n                else:\n                    self.display.executor_output(line)\n        if proc.returncode != 0:\n            if proc.stderr:\n                self.display.warn(f\"{label} stderr: {proc.stderr.strip()}\")\n            return False\n        return True\n\n    def _wait(self) -> None:\n        time.sleep(self.delay)\n","numLines":612,"startLine":1,"totalLines":612}}}

Strongest bet / most likely regret\n\n**Strongest: bet 2, the signal-contract switch.** Pool bodies write to a\nmanifest, only `min_success` at the join routes (`engine.py:368-379`,\n`contract.py:212-216` rejects bare signals in pool `on_signal`). This closes\na real v1 failure mode: v1's `_run_loop_parallel` decided per-item success by\nscanning for `next_item_signals` membership *or* `rc == 0`\n(`/tmp/v1_runner.py:180-186`) — an agent that emitted a stray signal-shaped\nstring in tool output could silently flip an item to done. v2's law (\"pool\nsignals are DATA, never route\", enforced at load time, not by convention) is\na structural fix, not a lint rule. (R)\n\n**Most likely to be regretted: bet 3, agent silence retries primary-only,\nnever falls back** (`classify.py:80-89`, README:117). The stated reason —\n\"another model drops the tag just as often; blind fallback duplicates side\neffects\" — is a real risk, but it's asymmetric: it protects against a\ndouble-write on a *stateful* body while guaranteeing that a *primary model\nhaving a bad day* (rate-limited, degraded, mis-following instructions) drains\nits entire `max_attempts` budget on itself and then hard-fails via\n`__default__`, even though the whole reason `fallback` exists is \"primary is\nunreliable, try someone else.\" A budget-gate retry-node can route around\n`__failed__`, but `__default__` is a distinct terminal with its own edge\n(README:340, `defaults.on_signal: {__failed__: notify, __default__: notify}`)\n— so silence-driven exhaustion needs its *own* handling, which most authors\nwill forget to add, because `fallback:` visually reads as \"the safety net for\nthis action\" and it silently isn't one for the single most common agent flake\nclass (README:117 calls silence \"the most common agent flake\"). One year of\nproduction use with prompts that drift or model updates that change tagging\nhabits will surface pipelines that fail hard on a fixable communication\nglitch, precisely the class of failure `fallback` was built to catch. (R for\nthe code path; G for the year-out prediction)\n\n## B. What v2 lost that tests can't show\n\n1. **Live terminal UX during a run.** v1's `output.py` (imported by\n`runner.py:9-13`) gave colored round banners, transition arrows, per-item\nparallel status lines (`ansi(..., BOLD+GREEN)`, `round_banner`,\n`round_stats`). v2's `log()` (`engine.py:56-57`) is one bare\n`[medulla] step N | node -> signal -> target` line to stderr. Functionally\nequivalent for the journal; materially worse for a human babysitting a long\nrun at a terminal — no coverage in the unit or live-test suite because none\nof it asserts terminal *output*, only structured outcomes. (R)\n\n2. **Cross-invocation persistent vars + real SIGTERM cleanup.** v1's\n`vars_map` synced to `.medulla/vars.<task>.yaml` on disk independent of any\nrun directory (`load_vars`/`save_var`, `runner.py`), and registered\n`atexit`/`SIGTERM` handlers (`_cleanup_bridge_bg`, `runner.py:200-270`) to\nkill background dev servers, stop docker containers, and clean bridge\nsockets on a *graceful* kill, not just SIGKILL. v2 explicitly deletes this\n(\"no finally... `kill -9` makes exit hooks an illusion\", README:306) and\nonly catches `KeyboardInterrupt` (`engine.py:941-944`) — SIGTERM is\nunhandled, so a pipeline that legitimately backgrounds a process (dev\nserver, emulator) and gets `docker stop`/systemd-SIGTERM'd leaks it. The\ncrash-only philosophy is defensible against `kill -9`, but SIGTERM was\ngraceful in v1 and is now treated identically to SIGKILL. The live-test\nsuite only checks SIGINT (`t14-interrupt`), not SIGTERM, so this gap is\ninvisible to it. (R)\n\n3. **Inline per-signal steps.** v1 allowed a transition to carry inline\n`runner:` steps or `reset_iterations` alongside the stage jump\n(`pipeline.py:70-79`, `_resolve_signal_target`). v2 forces every such action\ninto its own node+edge (README's \"handlers are ordinary nodes\"). Cleaner\ncontract, but it inflates small pipelines' node count for what used to be a\none-line hook — not tested either way since it's a authoring-ergonomics\ndelta, not a behavior delta.\n\n## C. One change before it calcifies\n\nSplit `__default__`'s routing from `__failed__`'s: **let silence use the\nfallback runner, gated behind an explicit opt-out**, rather than hard-wiring\n\"primary only, never fallback\" as the only mode. The manifest/journal already\nrecord `reason` per failure class (`recorded_signal`, `failure_class` in\n`AttemptsOutcome`), so an author who genuinely needs the current\nduplicate-avoidance guarantee (mutating body, side-effect-heavy) could opt in\nto \"no fallback on silence,\" while the default serves the common case\n(idempotent/read-mostly agent bodies) where blind fallback on silence is\nobviously better than a hard stop. Right now the contract picked the\nconservative branch for everyone and calls it done in README's frozen\ncontract — that's the one clause I'd unfreeze.\n\n## D. Verdict: deleting v1 outright\n\n**Right call, not hubris — for the actual conditions stated.** Single\nmaintainer, one production workflow, and a *documented* migration table\n(README:317-337) mapping every v1 primitive to its v2 equivalent is the\nopposite of hubris; it's the correct cost/benefit call when running a\ncompatibility shim (dual engines, dual test suites, dual mental models)\ncosts more than porting the one live pipeline by hand once. The panel-review\nprocess (audit references littered through the code — \"audit R1\", \"audit\nR3\", \"audit G7\", \"audit G8\", \"audit G9\" in `harness.py`, `procrun.py`,\n`engine.py`) shows the deletion was preceded by actually re-deriving v1's\nscars (agy `--print` token-eating, opencode's dead `--format json`, the\n`kill -9` orphan bug from `t14`) rather than dropping them. The one place\nthis reads as overconfidence rather than diligence is **bet 3** above: the\ncontract document calls itself \"frozen\" while shipping a debatable one-way\ndoor on silence-handling that the authors themselves flag as \"the most\ncommon agent flake\" — freezing a contract *before* a full production season\nunder real model-drift conditions is the part that could bite. The stated reason —\n\"another model drops the tag just as often; blind fallback duplicates side\neffects\" — is a real risk, but it's asymmetric: it protects against a\ndouble-write on a *stateful* body while guaranteeing that a *primary model\nhaving a bad day* (rate-limited, degraded, mis-following instructions) drains\nits entire `max_attempts` budget on itself and then hard-fails via\n`__default__`, even though the whole reason `fallback` exists is \"primary is\nunreliable, try someone else.\" A budget-gate retry-node can route around\n`__failed__`, but `__default__` is a distinct terminal with its own edge\n(README:340, `defaults.on_signal: {__failed__: notify, __default__: notify}`)\n— so silence-driven exhaustion needs its *own* handling, which most authors\nwill forget to add, because `fallback:` visually reads as \"the safety net for\nthis action\" and it silently isn't one for the single most common agent flake\nclass (README:117 calls silence \"the most common agent flake\"). One year of\nproduction use with prompts that drift or model updates that change tagging\nhabits will surface pipelines that fail hard on a fixable communication\nglitch, precisely the class of failure `fallback` was built to catch. (R for\nthe code path; G for the year-out prediction)\n\n## B. What v2 lost that tests can't show\n\n1. **Live terminal UX during a run.** v1's `output.py` (imported by\n`runner.py:9-13`) gave colored round banners, transition arrows, per-item\nparallel status lines (`ansi(..., BOLD+GREEN)`, `round_banner`,\n`round_stats`). v2's `log()` (`engine.py:56-57`) is one bare\n`[medulla] step N | node -> signal -> target` line to stderr. Functionally\nequivalent for the journal; materially worse for a human babysitting a long\nrun at a terminal — no coverage in the unit or live-test suite because none\nof it asserts terminal *output*, only structured outcomes. (R)\n\n2. **Cross-invocation persistent vars + real SIGTERM cleanup.** v1's\n`vars_map` synced to `.medulla/vars.<task>.yaml` on disk independent of any\nrun directory (`load_vars`/`save_var`, `runner.py`), and registered\n`atexit`/`SIGTERM` handlers (`_cleanup_bridge_bg`, `runner.py:200-270`) to\nkill background dev servers, stop docker containers, and clean bridge\nsockets on a *graceful* kill, not just SIGKILL. v2 explicitly deletes this\n(\"no finally... `kill -9` makes exit hooks an illusion\", README:306) and\nonly catches `KeyboardInterrupt` (`engine.py:941-944`) — SIGTERM is\nunhandled, so a pipeline that legitimately backgrounds a process (dev\nserver, emulator) and gets `docker stop`/systemd-SIGTERM'd leaks it. The\ncrash-only philosophy is defensible against `kill -9`, but SIGTERM was\ngraceful in v1 and is now treated identically to SIGKILL. The live-test\nsuite only checks SIGINT (`t14-interrupt`), not SIGTERM, so this gap is\ninvisible to it. (R)\n\n3. **Inline per-signal steps.** v1 allowed a transition to carry inline\n`runner:` steps or `reset_iterations` alongside the stage jump\n(`pipeline.py:70-79`, `_resolve_signal_target`). v2 forces every such action\ninto its own node+edge (README's \"handlers are ordinary nodes\"). Cleaner\ncontract, but it inflates small pipelines' node count for what used to be a\none-line hook — not tested either way since it's a authoring-ergonomics\ndelta, not a behavior delta.\n\n## C. One change before it calcifies\n\nSplit `__default__`'s routing from `__failed__`'s: **let silence use the\nfallback runner, gated behind an explicit opt-out**, rather than hard-wiring\n\"primary only, never fallback\" as the only mode. The manifest/journal already\nrecord `reason` per failure class (`recorded_signal`, `failure_class` in\n`AttemptsOutcome`), so an author who genuinely needs the current\nduplicate-avoidance guarantee (mutating body, side-effect-heavy) could opt in\nto \"no fallback on silence,\" while the default serves the common case\n(idempotent/read-mostly agent bodies) where blind fallback on silence is\nobviously better than a hard stop. Right now the contract picked the\nconservative branch for everyone and calls it done in README's frozen\ncontract — that's the one clause I'd unfreeze.\n\n## D. Verdict: deleting v1 outright\n\n**Right call, not hubris — for the actual conditions stated.** Single\nmaintainer, one production workflow, and a *documented* migration table\n(README:317-337) mapping every v1 primitive to its v2 equivalent is the\nopposite of hubris; it's the correct cost/benefit call when running a\ncompatibility shim (dual engines, dual test suites, dual mental models)\ncosts more than porting the one live pipeline by hand once. The panel-review\nprocess (audit references littered through the code — \"audit R1\", \"audit\nR3\", \"audit G7\", \"audit G8\", \"audit G9\" in `harness.py`, `procrun.py`,\n`engine.py`) shows the deletion was preceded by actually re-deriving v1's\nscars (agy `--print` token-eating, opencode's dead `--format json`, the\n`kill -9` orphan bug from `t14`) rather than dropping them. The one place\nthis reads as overconfidence rather than diligence is **bet 3** above: the\ncontract document calls itself \"frozen\" while shipping a debatable one-way\ndoor on silence-handling that the authors themselves flag as \"the most\ncommon agent flake\" — freezing a contract *before* a full production season\nunder real model-drift conditions is the part that could bite. (G)\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null,"userModified":false}}
